</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Wingdings',sans-serif;font-size:9pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#168;</span></div><div style="height:42.75pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="-sec-extract:summary;text-align:center"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:9pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">1</span></div></div></div><div id="i55322b507e0b4c21b43fc09236f34685_10"></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"/><div style="min-height:42.75pt;width:100%"><div><span><br/></span></div></div><div style="-sec-extract:summary;margin-bottom:9pt;padding-left:72pt;text-indent:-72pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Item 1.01</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Entry into a Material Definitive Agreement.</span></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">On November 25, 2024, Intel Corporation (&#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Intel</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;) entered into a direct funding agreement (the &#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Direct Funding Agreement</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;) with the U.S. Department of Commerce (the &#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">DOC</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;) under which the DOC agrees to award Intel funding under the Creating Helpful Incentives to Produce Semiconductors and Science Act of 2022 (the &#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">CHIPS Act</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;).</span></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Under the Direct Funding Agreement, the DOC has agreed to award Intel up to $7.8 billion in direct funding and $65 million in workforce development funding (collectively, the &#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Awards</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;) related to (i) the construction, modernization, tool purchase and installation in, and operation of, twelve microchip fabrication facilities and advanced packaging facilities located in Arizona, New Mexico, Ohio and Oregon (the &#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Projects</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;) and (ii) workforce activities related to the Projects.</span></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The DOC will disburse the Awards funding to Intel based on the achievement of various milestones, with each disbursement reimbursing Intel for eligible uses of funds already incurred and paid by Intel or its subsidiaries. Disbursements are Project-specific and subject to the achievement of various capital expenditure, facility completion, process technology development, wafer production, Intel products insourcing and external foundry customer acquisition milestones, the receipt of applicable permits and other governmental approvals, and various other conditions. </span></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The Direct Funding Agreement contains representations, warranties and covenants applicable to Intel and its affiliates that have direct or indirect ownership of any Project (those affiliates, together with Intel, the &#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Recipient Parties</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;), including with respect to (i) restrictions on dividends and share repurchases, (ii) restrictions on the expansion of semiconductor manufacturing capacity in certain foreign countries, (iii) restrictions on joint research and technology licensing with certain foreign entities, (iv) restrictions on the use or installation of prohibited equipment that is manufactured or assembled by certain foreign entities, (v) spending at least $35 billion on research and development within the United States cumulatively from 2024 through 2028, (vi) compliance with various federal regulations and requirements and (vii) limitations on dispositions of the Projects, including through dispositions of equity interests in the Projects. </span></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The Direct Funding Agreement contains restrictions on certain &#8220;change of control&#8221; transactions: (i) third party acquisition of 35% or more of the ownership of or voting rights with respect to Intel or otherwise acquiring control of Intel; (ii) Intel ceasing to own at least 50.1% of the ownership of or voting rights with respect to Intel Foundry if separated into a new legal entity (&#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Intel Foundry Corporation</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;) so long as Intel Foundry Corporation remains a private company; (iii) if Intel Foundry Corporation becomes a public company, third party acquisition of 35% or more of the ownership of or voting rights with respect to Intel Foundry Corporation at any time Intel is not its largest shareholder; (iv) Intel ceasing to have control of Intel Foundry Corporation; or (v) with respect to other Recipient Parties, Intel ceasing to own at least 50.1% of the ownership of or voting rights with respect to the Recipient Party equity or voting rights or otherwise ceasing to have control of the Recipient Party. Any &#8220;change of control&#8221; transaction must satisfy certain requirements as to the nature and financial resources of the counterparty, the impact to the creditworthiness of Intel and Intel Foundry Corporation, continued wafer purchases by Intel from Intel Foundry Corporation, and continuation of the Projects, the business strategy of manufacturing leading-edge semiconductors in the U.S. and the investment in U.S. semiconductor research and development, or would require DOC consent.</span></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Under the Direct Funding Agreement, Intel may be required to share with the DOC a percentage of the total cumulative realized unlevered free cash flow achieved by a Project (the &#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Project Return</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;) if it exceeds specified thresholds (the &#8220;</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Excess Return Sharing Requirement</span><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8221;). Any payments that may be required by Intel under the Excess Return Sharing Requirement are limited to a maximum of 75% of the Awards received by Intel for the applicable Project (after taking into account any clawbacks or other repayments of such Awards). Any Excess Return Sharing Requirement is separately calculated and applicable to a Project until the end of the ninth fiscal year following the fiscal year in which the Project Return for the Project is positive.</span></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">In the event of certain significant breaches under the Direct Funding Agreement by Intel and the other Recipient Parties (e.g., CHIPS Act program requirements, change of control restrictions, bankruptcy of Intel, etc.), the DOC may have termination rights and other remedies. Such rights and remedies vary depending on the nature of such breach, but can include: (i) requiring the repayment of some or all of the Awards; (ii) imposing additional conditions on the Awards; (iii) suspending or terminating all or any portion of the Awards; (iv) withholding or suspending a disbursement of the Awards; (v) terminating the Direct Funding Agreement and the Awards; and (vi) taking other actions available to the DOC.</span></div><div style="height:42.75pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="-sec-extract:summary;text-align:center"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:9pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">2</span></div></div></div><div id="i55322b507e0b4c21b43fc09236f34685_161"></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"/><div style="min-height:42.75pt;width:100%"><div><span><br/></span></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Item 7.01&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;Regulation FD Disclosure.</span></div><div><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">On November 26, 2024, Intel issued a press release announcing the entry into the Direct Funding Agreement. A copy of the press release is attached as Exhibit 99.1 and incorporated by this reference.</span></div><div><span><br/></span></div><div><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">The information in this Item 7.01 and Exhibit 99.1 shall not be deemed to be &#8220;filed&#8221; for purposes of Section 18 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the &#8220;</span><span reference into any filing under the Securities Act of 1933, as amended, or the Exchange Act.</span></div><div id="i55322b507e0b4c21b43fc09236f34685_13"></div><div style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Intel, Biden-Harris Administration Finalize $7.86 Billion Funding Award Under US CHIPS Act</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">Award to support Intel&#8217;s $100 billion investment plans to expand American semiconductor manufacturing and technology leadership.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:112%">NEWS HIGHLIGHTS </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%;padding-left:14.5pt">The U.S. Department of Commerce has awarded Intel up to $7.86 billion in direct funding through the U.S. CHIPS and Science Act to advance Intel&#8217;s commercial semiconductor manufacturing and advanced packaging projects in Arizona, New Mexico, Ohio and Oregon. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%;padding-left:14.5pt">This direct funding is in addition to the $3 billion contract awarded to Intel for the Secure Enclave program that is designed to expand trusted manufacturing of leading-edge semiconductors for the U.S. government.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%;padding-left:14.5pt">Today&#8217;s award, coupled with a 25% investment tax credit, will support Intel&#8217;s plans to invest more than $100 billion in the U.S. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%;padding-left:14.5pt">As previously announced, Intel&#8217;s planned U.S. investments, including projects beyond those supported by CHIPS, support more than 10,000 company jobs, nearly 20,000 construction jobs, and more than 50,000 indirect jobs with suppliers and supporting industries.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:112%">SANTA CLARA, Calif., Nov. 26, 2024 &#8211;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%"> Intel Corporation and the Biden-Harris Administration announced today that the U.S. Department of Commerce and Intel have reached agreement on terms to award the company up to $7.86 billion in direct funding for its commercial semiconductor manufacturing projects under the U.S. CHIPS and Science Act. The award will support Intel&#8217;s previously announced plans to advance critical semiconductor manufacturing and advanced packaging projects at its sites in Arizona, New Mexico, Ohio and Oregon. Intel also plans to claim the U.S. Treasury Department&#8217;s Investment Tax Credit, which is expected to be up to 25% of qualified investments of more than $100 billion.  </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8220;With Intel 3 already in high-volume production and Intel 18A set to follow next year, leading-edge semiconductors are once again being made on American soil,&#8221; said Pat Gelsinger, CEO of Intel. &#8220;Strong bipartisan support for restoring American technology and manufacturing leadership is driving historic investments that are critical to the country&#8217;s long-term economic growth and national security. Intel is deeply committed to advancing these shared priorities as we further expand our U.S. operations over the next several years.&#8221;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">The announcement demonstrates the U.S. government&#8217;s confidence in Intel&#8217;s essential role in building a resilient, trusted semiconductor supply chain on domestic soil. Since the passage of the CHIPS and Science Act more than two years ago, Intel has announced plans to invest more than $100 billion in the U.S. to expand chipmaking and advanced packaging capacity and capabilities critical to economic and national security. The historic investments will support tens of thousands of jobs, strengthen U.S. supply chains, foster U.S.-based R&#38;D, and help ensure American leadership in cutting-edge semiconductor manufacturing and technology capabilities.</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8220;The CHIPS for America program will supercharge American technology and innovation and make our country more secure &#8211; and Intel is expected to play an important role in the revitalization of the U.S. semiconductor industry,&#8221; said U.S. Secretary of Commerce Gina Raimondo. &#8220;Thanks to the leadership of President Biden and Vice President Harris, our CHIPS award is catalyzing Intel to make one of the largest investments in semiconductor manufacturing in U.S. history.&#8221;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">The award follows the previously signed preliminary memorandum of terms and the completion of Commerce&#8217;s due diligence, in addition to the announced investment tax credit. The final total award is less than the proposed preliminary award due to a congressional requirement to use CHIPS funding to pay for the $3 billion Secure Enclave program.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:112%">Press Kit&#58;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%"> U.S. CHIPS Act Funding for Intel</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:112%">U.S. Manufacturing and R&#38;D Investments</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">The CHIPS Act award will directly support Intel&#8217;s investments at sites where the company develops and produces many of the world&#8217;s most advanced chips and semiconductor packaging technologies, including in Arizona, the Silicon Desert&#59; New Mexico, the Silicon Mesa&#59; Ohio, the Silicon Heartland&#59; and Oregon, the Silicon Forest.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%;padding-left:14.5pt">Arizona&#58; Intel&#8217;s U.S. Manufacturing Powerhouse (Silicon Desert Fact Sheet)</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%;padding-left:14.5pt">New Mexico&#58; Intel&#8217;s U.S. Advanced Packaging Site (Silicon Mesa Fact Sheet)</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%;padding-left:14.5pt">Ohio&#58; Intel&#8217;s New Leading-Edge Manufacturing Site (Silicon Heartland Fact Sheet)</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%;padding-left:14.5pt">Oregon&#58; The Heart of Intel&#8217;s Semiconductor R&#38;D (Silicon Forest Fact Sheet)</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">Intel was founded in the U.S. and has been innovating, investing and supporting global semiconductor manufacturing and R&#38;D for more than 50 years. Intel currently employs approximately 45,000 people in the U.S.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:112%">Foundry Momentum and Technology Leadership</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">Intel is nearing completion of a historic pace of semiconductor node development to regain process technology leadership. Intel 18A, the company&#8217;s fifth process node in four years, is on track to launch in 2025 and continues to gain traction with customers. The company is finalizing a multiyear, multibillion-dollar commitment by Amazon Web Services to expand its existing partnership to include a new custom Intel&#174; Xeon&#174; 6 chip on Intel 3 and a new AI fabric chip on Intel 18A.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">In September 2024, Intel won a manufacturing contract for up to $3 billion for the Secure Enclave program. This program is designed to expand the trusted manufacturing of leading-edge semiconductors for the U.S. government and builds on Intel&#8217;s relationship with the U.S. Department of Defense through the Rapid Assured Microelectronics Prototypes - Commercial (RAMP-C) and State-of-the-Art Heterogeneous Integrated Packaging (SHIP) programs.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">Additionally, Intel reported key milestones in advanced semiconductor manufacturing with the completed assembly of the industry&#8217;s first commercial High Numerical Aperture (High NA) Extreme Ultraviolet (EUV) lithography scanner and receipt of an additional High NA tool installed at the company&#8217;s Hillsboro, Oregon, R&#38;D site. This will enable Intel to lead cutting-edge advancements that will define next-generation chip manufacturing.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:112%">Workforce Development and Childcare Benefits</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">Alongside its manufacturing and technology investments, Intel has a long-standing history of investing in the American workforce by supporting education, training and benefits programs needed to create the jobs of the future. In 2022, for example, Intel announced a $100 million investment to expand semiconductor education, research and workforce training opportunities across the nation.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">As part of Intel&#8217;s overall CHIPS award, $65 million is set aside to support the company&#8217;s efforts to create a more skilled semiconductor workforce. Intel plans to use $56 million to help train students and faculty at all education levels to support industry growth. This includes, for example, Intel&#8217;s recently launched U.S. registered apprenticeship program for manufacturing facility technicians.</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">The company will use $5 million of the dedicated workforce award to help increase childcare availability near Intel&#8217;s facilities. This is intended to support Intel&#8217;s recently announced plans to broaden childcare benefits and pilot innovative programs to support working families. The remaining $4 million of the $65 million award will support Intel&#8217;s participation in the CHIPS Women in Construction Framework, which Intel voluntarily committed to this year to help expand the construction workforce by increasing the participation of women and economically disadvantaged individuals.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">Finally, Intel is partnering with the Midwest Microelectronics Consortium (MMEC) as its members receive funding for five technology development projects within the Microelectronics Commons initiative established under the CHIPS Act. These projects will engage more than 30 MMEC members representing organizations from industry, academia and government stakeholders to advance domestic microelectronic technology development to deliver solutions to strengthen the U.S.-based supply chain.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:112%">***</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:112%;text-decoration:underline">Forward-Looking Statements</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">This release contains forward-looking statements that involve a number of risks and uncertainties.
